Full English breakfasts are awesome to eat when you're hungover. Keep in mind, the beauty of this breakfast is that you can customise it any way you want. You can drop the mushrooms, (if you're that crazy) drop the black puddings, use scrambled eggs, use beef tomatoes or chopped tomatoes from a tin. And contrary to what you might believe, you don't need a big cast iron flat top, it can all be done on regular sized frying pan. In fact some pans are designed specifically for full english breakfasts over here. Also, hash browns are way more popular than bubble and squeaks, and a glass of orange juice is a perfect drink to compliment the saltiness of this meal.

Born, bred and live in England. Any place serving a "Full English", won't include bubble and squeak.  Maybe a hash brown, but definitely not bubble and squeak. Its definitely part of the English repertoire, but not authentic  for a full breakfast.  The tomatoes would be tinned plum tomatoes more commonly. If using fresh tomato, then its usually one half of a slicer  that's been grilled (broiled).  The bacon is usually cooked a little more crispy too. Black pudding is usually only seen on a "Full Scottish", not the English version. Our fried eggs are only cooked on one side.

I understand that the culinary industry in the US is to blame for falsely calling ham "Canadian Bacon", but those slices of ham are NOT what we in Canada call bacon or Canadian bacon. Real Canadian Bacon is taken from the same part of the pig as English Bacon, except ours is then cured and rolled in peameal, and thus we call it "Peameal Bacon" or "Back Bacon". But please for the sake of my country stop calling fried slices of ham Canadian Bacon, because it just isn't.
